## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics / demographic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics (density-independent vs density-dependent growth, environmental forcing, harvesting/immigration). With only (t, P) available, common structures are autonomous or time-forced ordinary differential equations in P.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Affine growth with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (constant net influx/outflux plus proportional growth)
- Logistic ODE (quadratic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation via crowding)
- General quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (phenomenological per-capita growth decreasing linearly with P when c1<0)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases with log of size; common for microbial/tumor growth)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density regulation)
- Richards-type form (generalized logistic in ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (alternative parameterization of generalized saturation)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic near low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low density plus carrying-capacity limitation)
- Weak Allee effect (rational boost at low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P) / (P + c3) (reduced mating/coop at low P without forcing extinction)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (harvest/removal independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting (constant effort): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to population size)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II catch): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (limited harvesting capacity at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P (time-varying per-capita growth due to seasonality)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (resource-driven K(t) oscillations; written with allowed constant placement)
- Secular trend / regime shift: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (long-term change in growth conditions with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth modeling: rewrite as (dP_dt) / P = g(P, t); linear g(P)=c0 implies exponential growth, while decreasing g(P) indicates density dependence
- Crowding/self-limitation: negative P**2 contribution in dP_dt (or negative slope in per-capita growth vs P) captures competition for resources/space
- Carrying capacity as a root: factors like (1 - c * P) imply an equilibrium near P Ōēł 1/c where growth switches sign
- Allee effects: an additional low-P root (e.g., (c*P - 1) factor) creates negative growth below a threshold and possible bistability
- Gompertz/log regulation: log(c/P) terms imply multiplicative growth with diminishing returns that weaken roughly with log size
- Harvesting signatures: subtractive terms (ŌłÆc, ŌłÆc*P, or ŌłÆc*P/(P+c)) indicate external removal; their P-dependence suggests constant-yield vs effort-limited harvest
- Seasonal/environmental forcing: periodic dependence on t (sin/cos) indicates cyclic birth/death rates or resource availability; can modulate r(t) or K(t)
- Nonautonomous drift: inclusion of t in coefficients (c0 + c1*t) suggests gradual environmental change or management interventions over time
- Multiple equilibria and thresholds: polynomial factorizations in P (product of linear terms) often signal distinct stable/unstable equilibrium points in population dynamics

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 80

Let \(F(P)\) be the Ground Truth (GT). Note GT has **no \(t\)** dependence and equals
\[
F(P)=0.1699888\Big[(-1+P/1.047284)(1-P/10.210545)P+(1-P/10.210545)P+(1-e^{-0.09709294P})P\Big].
\]
So \(F(P)\) is a sum of:
- a **cubic polynomial** in \(P\) (from the first two bracketed terms), plus
- a **non-polynomial term** \(0.1699888\,(1-e^{-kP})P\) with \(k=0.09709294\), i.e. it contains \(P e^{-kP}\).

Therefore any matching candidate must be able (after choosing its constants) to produce a term proportional to \(P e^{-kP}\) (or equivalently \(P - P e^{-kP}\)), and must not introduce unavoidable \(t\)-dependence, logs, abs, trig, rational singularities, etc.

Now check candidates:

1. Has \(\sin(c7 t+c8)\) and \(\log\) terms. To remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\), but logs remain unless their coefficients are 0; then expression becomes polynomial \(P^2c0+Pc5+c9\). Cannot create \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.

2. Pure algebraic powers + \(\log(\,|P|\,)\). Logs must be killed \(\Rightarrow c6=0\). Remaining is polynomial/power \(P^{c4}\). No \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.

3. Polynomial + \(\log\). Kill log by \(c8=0\). Still polynomial/power only. **No**.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(ŌłÆ1 + P/1.047)*(1 ŌłÆ P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 ŌłÆ P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 ŌłÆ exp(ŌłÆ0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:

**Term 1:** `0.17*(P/1.047 ŌłÆ 1)*(1 ŌłÆ P/10.21)*P`
= 0.17*(P/1.047 ŌłÆ 1)*(P ŌłÆ P┬▓/10.21)
= 0.17*[(P┬▓/1.047 ŌłÆ P) ŌłÆ (P┬│/(1.047┬Ę10.21) ŌłÆ P┬▓/10.21)]
= 0.17*[P┬▓/1.047 ŌłÆ P ŌłÆ P┬│/10.70 + P┬▓/10.21]

**Term 2:** `0.17*(1 ŌłÆ P/10.21)*P`
= 0.17*(P ŌłÆ P┬▓/10.21)

**Term 3:** `0.17*(1 ŌłÆ exp(ŌłÆ0.097*P))*P`
= 0.17*(P ŌłÆ P┬Ęexp(ŌłÆ0.097*P))

Combining Terms 1+2+3:

From Term 1: 0.17*[P┬▓/1.047 ŌłÆ P ŌłÆ P┬│/10.70 + P┬▓/10.21]
From Term 2: 0.17*[P ŌłÆ P┬▓/10.21]
From Term 3: 0.17*[P ŌłÆ P┬Ęexp(ŌłÆ0.097*P)]

Adding:
- P┬│ terms: ŌłÆ0.17*P┬│/10.70 = ŌłÆ0.01589*P┬│
- P┬▓ terms: 0.17*P┬▓/1.047 + 0.17*P┬▓/10.21 ŌłÆ 0.17*P┬▓/10.21 = 0.17*P┬▓/1.047 Ōēł 0.1623*P┬▓
- P terms: ŌłÆ0.17P + 0.17P + 0.17P = 0.17P
- exp terms: ŌłÆ0.17*P*exp(ŌłÆ0.097*P)

So GT Ōēł **cŌéü┬ĘP┬│ + cŌéé┬ĘP┬▓ + cŌéā┬ĘP + cŌéä┬ĘP┬Ęexp(cŌéģ┬ĘP)**

where cŌéģ < 0. The key basis functions are: **P┬│, P┬▓, P, P┬Ęexp(ŌłÆ╬▒P)**.

Now I need to check which candidates can express this combination of basis functions.

The critical element is the **P┬Ęexp(ŌłÆ╬▒P)** term. Let me check which candidates have an exponential-like term that could produce this.

Most candidates use `log(c*|P| + 1)` or `log(c*exp(P*c) + 1)` instead of `exp(c*P)`. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me identify candidates with `exp(c*P)` terms (not wrapped in log, cos, sin, etc.):

- **Candidate 11**: has `c5*exp(P*c6)` ŌĆö This gives a pure exp(cP), not P┬Ęexp(cP). Cannot match.
- **Candidate 42**: `c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1)` ŌĆö This is a softplus, not exp.
- **Candidate 63**: `c4*exp(P*c5)` ŌĆö pure exp, not P┬Ęexp.
- **Candidate 69, 70, 79**: have `c3*exp(P*c4)` ŌĆö pure exp, not P┬Ęexp.

None of the candidates have a `P*exp(c*P)` term explicitly. The GT requires this basis function, and it cannot be constructed from polynomials, logs, sins, or pure exponentials.

Let me verify: can `log(c*exp(cP)+1)` approximate `P*exp(cP)`? No ŌĆö these are fundamentally different functions. Can any combination of the offered basis functions exactly equal `P*exp(cP)`? No ŌĆö exponentials, polynomials, logs, and trig functions are linearly independent from `P*exp(cP)`.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the required `P┬Ęexp(c┬ĘP)` basis function. Since this term cannot be zeroed (it has a specific nonzero coefficient in the GT), no candidate can match.

Going through all 80 candidates systematically, none contain `P*exp(c*P)` as a basis function.
